- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls

# Investigation: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/prometheus--ba14bc4 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/prometheus--ba14bc4 (mirror of prometheus/prometheus)
**Task Type:** Cross-Service Debug (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

After a Prometheus upgrade, remote-write destinations intermittently stop receiving samples. The issue correlates with target discovery changes — when targets are added or removed, some remote-write shards stall.

Prometheus logs show:
```
level=info msg="Resharding queues" from=4 to=6
level=info msg="Resharding done" numShards=6
```

But after resharding, metrics show some shards have `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` stuck at >0 with no progress.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. How remote-write queue resharding works (which files/functions)
2. What changed in the resharding logic recently
3. The specific mechanism causing shards to stall
4. Why the issue is intermittent (timing/race condition)
5. Which metrics or logs would confirm the root cause

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy and diagnostic steps>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on `storage/remote/` package, particularly queue management and shard calculation

58-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive investigation of the remote-write queue resharding failure. Here's what I found:

## Key Findings

**Root Cause**: During resharding when target discovery changes occur, samples in flight are **permanently dropped** if the flush deadline expires before all pending samples can be sent. This creates a silent data loss scenario where:

1. `reshardLoop()` initiates shard replacement by calling `stop()` → `start()`
2. `stop()` waits up to 1 minute (`flushDeadline`) for queues to gracefully flush
3. If the deadline expires, `hardShutdown()` is triggered
4. All remaining samples are dropped (lines 1575-1577 in queue_manager.go) without being sent or recovered
5. New shards start with a different hash distribution, making recovery impossible
6. Metrics show `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` stuck at >0 with no progress

**Why It's Intermittent**: The issue depends on:
- **Load**: Higher sample rates fill queues faster, requiring more flush time
- **Network**: Slow remote endpoints delay sends
- **Target discovery timing**: Changes coincide with high load or network issues

The investigation report includes detailed code references, evidence from the CHANGELOG, diagnostic metrics/logs to confirm the issue, and recommended fix strategies. The report has been written to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` and covers all required sections without proposing any code modifications.

interface for sending a batch of samples to an\n404: // external timeseries database.\n405: type WriteClient interface {\n406: \t// Store stores the given samples in the remote storage.\n407: \tStore(ctx context.Context, req []byte, retryAttempt int) (WriteResponseStats, error)\n408: \t// Name uniquely identifies the remote storage.\n409: \tName() string\n410: \t// Endpoint is the remote read or write endpoint for the storage client.\n411: \tEndpoint() string\n412: }\n413: \n414: // QueueManager manages a queue of samples to be sent to the Storage\n415: // indicated by the provided WriteClient. Implements writeTo interface\n416: // used by WAL Watcher.\n417: type QueueManager struct {\n418: \tlastSendTimestamp            atomic.Int64\n419: \tbuildRequestLimitTimestamp   atomic.Int64\n420: \treshardDisableStartTimestamp atomic.Int64 // Time that reshard was disabled.\n421: \treshardDisableEndTimestamp   atomic.Int64 // Time that reshard is disabled until.\n422: \n423: \tlogger                  *slog.Logger\n424: \tflushDeadline           time.Duration\n425: \tcfg                     config.QueueConfig\n426: \tmcfg                    config.MetadataConfig\n427: \texternalLabels          []labels.Label\n428: \trelabelConfigs          []*relabel.Config\n429: \tsendExemplars           bool\n430: \tsendNativeHistograms    bool\n431: \tenableTypeAndUnitLabels bool\n432: \twatcher                 *wlog.Watcher\n433: \tmetadataWatcher         *MetadataWatcher\n434: \n435: \tclientMtx   sync.RWMutex\n436: \tstoreClient WriteClient\n437: \tprotoMsg    config.RemoteWriteProtoMsg\n438: \tcompr       compression.Type\n439: \n440: \tseriesMtx      sync.Mutex // Covers seriesLabels, seriesMetadata, droppedSeries and builder.\n441: \tseriesLabels   map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]labels.Labels\n442: \tseriesMetadata map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]*metadata.Metadata\n443: \tdroppedSeries  map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]struct{}\n444: \tbuilder        *labels.Builder\n445: \n446: \tseriesSegmentMtx     sync.Mutex // Covers seriesSegmentIndexes - if you also lock seriesMtx, take seriesMtx first.\n447: \tseriesSegmentIndexes map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]int\n448: \n449: \tshards      *shards\n450: \tnumShards   int\n451: \treshardChan chan int\n452: \tquit        chan struct{}\n453: \twg          sync.WaitGroup\n454: \n455: \tdataIn, dataOut, dataOutDuration *ewmaRate\n456: \n457: \tmetrics  *queueManagerMetrics\n458: \tinterner *pool\n459: }\n460: \n461: // NewQueueManager builds a new QueueManager and starts a new\n462: // WAL watcher with queue manager as the WriteTo destination.\n463: // The WAL watcher takes the dir parameter as the base directory\n464: // for where the WAL shall be located. Note that the full path to\n465: // the WAL directory will be constructed as <dir>/wal.\n466: func NewQueueManager(\n467: \tmetrics *queueManagerMetrics,\n468: \twatcherMetrics *wlog.WatcherMetrics,\n469: \treaderMetrics *wlog.LiveReaderMetrics,\n470: \tlogger *slog.Logger,\n471: \tdir string,\n472: \tcfg config.QueueConfig,\n473: \tmCfg config.MetadataConfig,\n474: \texternalLabels labels.Labels,\n475: \trelabelConfigs []*relabel.Config,\n476: \tclient WriteClient,\n477: \tflushDeadline time.Duration,\n478: \tinterner *pool,\n479: \tsm ReadyScrapeManager,\n480: \tenableExemplarRemoteWrite bool,\n481: \tenableNativeHistogramRemoteWrite bool,\n482: \tenableTypeAndUnitLabels bool,\n483: \tprotoMsg config.RemoteWriteProtoMsg,\n484: ) *QueueManager {\n485: \tif logger == nil {\n486: \t\tlogger = promslog.NewNopLogger()\n487: \t}\n488: \n489: \t// Copy externalLabels into a slice, which we need for processExternalLabels.\n490: \textLabelsSlice := make([]labels.Label, 0, externalLabels.Len())\n491: \texternalLabels.Range(func(l labels.Label) {\n492: \t\textLabelsSlice = append(extLabelsSlice, l)\n493: \t})\n494: \n495: \tlogger = logger.With(remoteName, client.Name(), endpoint, client.Endpoint())\n496: \tt := &QueueManager{\n497: \t\tlogger:                  logger,\n498: \t\tflushDeadline:           flushDeadline,\n499: \t\tcfg:                     cfg,\n500: \t\tmcfg:                    mCfg,\n501: \t\texternalLabels:          extLabelsSlice,\n502: \t\trelabelConfigs:          relabelConfigs,\n503: \t\tstoreClient:             client,\n504: \t\tsendExemplars:           enableExemplarRemoteWrite,\n505: \t\tsendNativeHistograms:    enableNativeHistogramRemoteWrite,\n506: \t\tenableTypeAndUnitLabels: enableTypeAndUnitLabels,\n507: \n508: \t\tseriesLabels:         make(map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]labels.Labels),\n509: \t\tseriesMetadata:       make(map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]*metadata.Metadata),\n510: \t\tseriesSegmentIndexes: make(map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]int),\n511: \t\tdroppedSeries:        make(map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]struct{}),\n512: \t\tbuilder:              labels.NewBuilder(labels.EmptyLabels()),\n513: \n514: \t\tnumShards:   cfg.MinShards,\n515: \t\treshardChan: make(chan int),\n516: \t\tquit:        make(chan struct{}),\n517: \n518: \t\tdataIn: \n522: \t\tmetrics:  metrics,\n523: \t\tinterner: interner,\n524: \n525: \t\tprotoMsg: protoMsg,\n526: \t\tcompr:    compression.Snappy, // Hardcoded for now, but scaffolding exists for likely future use.\n527: \t}\n528: \n529: \twalMetadata := t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1\n530: \n531: \tt.watcher = wlog.NewWatcher(watcherMetrics, readerMetrics, logger, client.Name(), t, dir, enableExemplarRemoteWrite, enableNativeHistogramRemoteWrite, walMetadata)\n532: \n533: \t// The current MetadataWatcher implementation is mutually exclusive\n534: \t// with the new approach, which stores metadata as WAL records and\n535: \t// ships them alongside series. If both mechanisms are set, the new one\n536: \t// takes precedence by implicitly disabling the older one.\n537: \tif t.mcfg.Send && t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1 {\n538: \t\tlogger.Warn(\"usage of 'metadata_config.send' is redundant when using remote write v2 (or higher) as metadata will always be gathered from the WAL and included for every series within each write request\")\n539: \t\tt.mcfg.Send = false\n540: \t}\n541: \n542: \tif t.mcfg.Send {\n543: \t\tt.metadataWatcher = NewMetadataWatcher(logger, sm, client.Name(), t, t.mcfg.SendInterval, flushDeadline)\n544: \t}\n545: \tt.shards = t.newShards()\n546: \n547: \treturn t\n548: }\n549: \n550: // AppendWatcherMetadata sends metadata to the remote storage. Metadata is sent in batches, but is not parallelized.\n551: // This is only used for the metadata_config.send setting and 1.x Remote Write.\n552: func (t *QueueManager) AppendWatcherMetadata(ctx context.Context, metadata []scrape.MetricMetadata) {\n553: \t// no op for any newer proto format, which will cache metadata sent to it from the WAL watcher.\n554: \tif t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1 {\n555: \t\treturn\n556: \t}\n557: \n558: \t// 1.X will still get metadata in batches.\n559: \tmm := make([]prompb.MetricMetadata, 0, len(metadata))\n560: \tfor _, entry := range metadata {\n561: \t\tmm = append(mm, prompb.MetricMetadata{\n562: \t\t\tMetricFamilyName: entry.MetricFamily,\n563: \t\t\tHelp:             entry.Help,\n564: \t\t\tType:             prompb.FromMetadataType(entry.Type),\n565: \t\t\tUnit:             entry.Unit,\n566: \t\t})\n567: \t}\n568: \n569: \tpBuf := proto.NewBuffer(nil)\n570: \tnumSends := int(math.Ceil(float64(len(metadata)) / float64(t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend)))\n571: \tfor i := range numSends {\n572: \t\tlast := min((i+1)*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend, len(metadata))\n573: \t\terr := t.sendMetadataWithBackoff(ctx, mm[i*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend:last], pBuf)\n574: \t\tif err != nil {\n575: \t\t\tt.metrics.failedMetadataTotal.Add(float64(last - (i * t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend)))\n576: \t\t\tt.logger.Error(\"non-recoverable error while sending metadata\", \"count\", last-(i*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend), \"err\", err)\n577: \t\t}\n578: \t}\n579: }\n580: \n581: func (t *QueueManager) sendMetadataWithBackoff(ctx context.Context, metadata []prompb.MetricMetadata, pBuf *proto.Buffer) error {\n582: \t// Build the WriteRequest with no samples (v1 flow).\n583: \treq, _, _, err := buildWriteRequest(t.logger, nil, metadata, pBuf, nil, nil, t.compr)\n584: \tif err != nil {\n585: \t\treturn err\n586: \t}\n587: \n588: \tmetadataCount := len(metadata)\n589: \n590: \tattemptStore := func(try int) error {\n591: \t\tctx, span := otel.Tracer(\"\").Start(ctx, \"Remote Metadata Send Batch\")\n592: \t\tdefer span.End()\n593: \n594: \t\tspan.SetAttributes(\n595: \t\t\tattribute.Int(\"metadata\", metadataCount),\n596: \t\t\tattribute.Int(\"try\", try),\n597: \t\t\tattribute.String(\"remote_name\", t.storeClient.Name()),\n598: \t\t\tattribute.String(\"remote_url\", t.storeClient.Endpoint()),\n599: \t\t)\n600: \t\t// Attributes defined by OpenTelemetry semantic conventions.\n601: \t\tif try > 0 {\n602: \t\t\tspan.SetAttributes(semconv.HTTPResendCount(try))\n603: \t\t}\n604: \n605: \t\tbegin := time.Now()\n606: \t\t// Ignoring WriteResponseStats, because there is nothing for metadata, since it's\n607: \t\t// embedded in v2 calls now, and we do v1 here.\n608: \t\t_, err := t.storeClient.Store(ctx, req, try)\n609: \t\tt.metrics.sentBatchDuration.Observe(time.Since(begin).Seconds())\n610: \n611: \t\tif err != nil {\n612: \t\t\tspan.RecordError(err)\n613: \t\t\treturn err\n614: \t\t}\n615: \t\treturn nil\n616: \t}\n617: \n618: \tretry := func() {\n619: \t\tt.metrics.retriedMetadataTotal.Add(float64(len(metadata)))\n620: \t}\n621: \terr = t.sendWriteRequestWithBackoff(ctx, attemptStore, retry)\n622: \tif err != nil {\n623: \t\treturn err\n624: \t}\n625: \tt.metrics.metadataTotal.Add(float64(len(metadata)))\n626: \tt.metrics.metadataBytesTotal.Add(float64(len(req)))\n627: \treturn nil\n628: }\n629: \n630: func isSampleOld(baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration, ts int64) bool {\n631: \tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n632: \t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we never skip samples due to their age.\n633: \t\treturn false\n634: \t}\n635: \tlimitTs := baseTime.Add(-sampleAgeLimit)\n636: \tsampleTs := timestamp.Time(ts)\n637: \treturn sampleTs.Before(limitTs)\n638: }\n639: \n640: func isTimeSeriesOldFilter(metrics *queueManagerMetrics, baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration) func(ts prompb.TimeSeries) bool {\n641: \treturn func(ts prompb.TimeSeries) bool {\n642: \t\tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n643: \t\t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we never skip samples due to their age.\n644: \t\t\treturn false\n645: \t\t}\n646: \t\tswitch {\n647: \t\t// Only the first element should be set in the series, therefore we only check the first element.\n648: \t\tcase len(ts.Samples) > 0:\n649: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, sampleAgeLimit, ts.Samples[0].Timestamp) {\n650: \t\t\t\tmetrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n651: \t\t\t\treturn true\n652: \t\t\t}\n653: \t\tcase len(ts.Histograms) > 0:\n654: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, sampleAgeLimit, ts.Histograms[0].Timestamp) {\n655: \t\t\t\tmetrics.droppedHistogramsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n656: \t\t\t\treturn true\n657: \t\t\t}\n658: \t\tcase len(ts.Exemplars) > 0:\n659: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, sampleAgeLimit, ts.Exemplars[0].Timestamp) {\n660: \t\t\t\tmetrics.droppedExemplarsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n661: \t\t\t\treturn true\n662: \t\t\t}\n663: \t\tdefault:\n664: \t\t\treturn false\n665: \t\t}\n666: \t\treturn false\n667: \t}\n668: }\n669: \n670: func isV2TimeSeriesOldFilter(metrics *queueManagerMetrics, baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration) func(ts writev2.TimeSeries) bool {\n671: \treturn func(ts writev2.TimeSeries) bool {\n672: \t\tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n673: \t\t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we never skip samples due to their age.\n674: \t\t\treturn false\n675: \t\t}\n676: \t\tswitch {\n677: \t\t// Only the first element should be set in the series, therefore we only check the first element.\n678: \t\tcase len(ts.Samples) > 0:\n679: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, sampleAgeLimit, ts.Samples[0].Timestamp) {\n680: \t\t\t\tmetrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n681: \t\t\t\treturn true\n682: \t\t\t}\n683: \t\tcase len(ts.Histograms) > 0:\n684: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, sampleAgeLimit, ts.Histograms[0].Timestamp) {\n685: \t\t\t\tmetrics.droppedHistogramsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n686: \t\t\t\treturn true\n687: \t\t\t}\n688: \t\tcase len(ts.Exemplars) > 0:\n689: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, sampleAgeLimit, ts.Exemplars[0].Timestamp) {\n690: \t\t\t\tmetrics.droppedExemplarsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n691: \t\t\t\treturn true\n692: \t\t\t}\n693: \t\tdefault:\n694: \t\t\treturn false\n695: \t\t}\n696: \t\treturn false\n697: \t}\n698: }\n699: \n700: // Append queues a sample to be sent to the remote storage. Blocks until all samples are\n701: // enqueued on their shards or a shutdown signal is received.\n702: func (t *QueueManager) Append(samples []record.RefSample) bool {\n703: \tcurrentTime := time.Now()\n704: outer:\n705: \tfor _, s := range samples {\n706: \t\tif isSampleOld(currentTime, time.Duration(t.cfg.SampleAgeLimit), s.T) {\n707: \t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n708: \t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t}\n710: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n711: \t\tlbls, ok := t.seriesLabels[s.Ref]\n712: \t\tif !ok {\n713: \t\t\tif _, ok := t.droppedSeries[s.Ref]; !ok {\n714: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Dropped sample for series that was not explicitly dropped via relabelling\", \"ref\", s.Ref)\n715: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonUnintentionalDroppedSeries).Inc()\n716: \t\t\t} else {\n717: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonDroppedSeries).Inc()\n718: \t\t\t}\n719: \t\t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n720: \t\t\tcontinue\n721: \t\t}\n722: \t\t// TODO(cstyan): Handle or at least log an error if no metadata is found.\n723: \t\t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n724: \t\tmeta := t.seriesMetadata[s.Ref]\n725: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n726: \t\t// Start with a very small backoff. \t\t\t\treturn false\n735: \t\t\tdefault:\n736: \t\t\t}\n737: \t\t\tif t.shards.enqueue(s.Ref, timeSeries{\n738: \t\t\t\tseriesLabels: lbls,\n739: \t\t\t\tmetadata:     meta,\n740: \t\t\t\ttimestamp: \tt.metrics.maxNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MaxShards))\n930: \tt.metrics.minNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MinShards))\n931: \tt.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MinShards))\n932: and waits for pending\n946: // sends to complete.\n947: func (t *QueueManager) Stop() {\n948: \tt.logger.Info(\"Stopping remote storage...\")\n949: \tdefer t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage stopped.\")\n950: \n951: \tclose(t.quit)\n952: \tt.wg.Wait()\n953: \t// Wait for all QueueManager routines to end before stopping shards, metadata watcher, and WAL watcher. This\n954: \t// is to ensure we don't end up executing a reshard and shards.stop() at the same time, which\n955: \t// causes a closed channel panic.\n956: \tt.shards.stop()\n957: for lookups when sending samples to remote.\n965: func (t *QueueManager) StoreSeries(series []record.RefSeries, index int) {\n966: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n967: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n968: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n969: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n970: \tfor _, s := range series {\n971: \t\t// Just make sure all the Refs of Series will insert into seriesSegmentIndexes map \t}\n1001: }\n1002: \n1003: // UpdateSeriesSegment updates the segment number held against the series,\n1004: // so we can trim older ones in SeriesReset.\n1005: func (t *QueueManager) UpdateSeriesSegment(series []record.RefSeries, index int) {\n1006: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n1007: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n1008: \tfor _, s := range series {\n1009: \t\tt.seriesSegmentIndexes[s.Ref] = index\n1010: \t}\n1011: }\n1012: \n1013: // SeriesReset is used when reading a checkpoint. WAL Watcher should have\n1014: // stored series records with the checkpoints index number, so we can now\n1015: // delete any ref ID's lower than that # from the two maps.\n1016: func (t *QueueManager) SeriesReset(index int) {\n1017: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n1018: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n1019: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n1020: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n1021: \t// Check for series that are in segments older than the checkpoint\n1022: \t// that were not also present in the checkpoint.\n1023: \tfor k, v := range t.seriesSegmentIndexes {\n1024: \t\tif v < index {\n1025: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesSegmentIndexes, k)\n1026: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesLabels, k)\n1027: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesMetadata, k)\n1028: \t\t\tdelete(t.droppedSeries, k)\n1029: \t\t}\n1030: \t}\n1031: }\n1032: \n1033: // SetClient updates the client used by a queue. Used when only client specific\n1034: // fields are updated to avoid restarting the queue.\n1035: func (t *QueueManager) SetClient(c WriteClient) {\n1036: \tt.clientMtx.Lock()\n1037: \tt.storeClient = c\n1038: \tt.clientMtx.Unlock()\n1039: }\n1040: \n1041: func (t *QueueManager) client() WriteClient {\n1042: \tt.clientMtx.RLock()\n1043: \tdefer t.clientMtx.RUnlock()\n1044: \treturn t.storeClient\n1045: }\n1046: \n1047: // processExternalLabels merges externalLabels into b. If b contains\n1048: // a label in externalLabels, the value in b wins.\n1049: func processExternalLabels(b *labels.Builder, externalLabels []labels.Label) {\n1050: \tfor _, el := range externalLabels {\n1051: \t\tif b.Get(el.Name) == \"\" {\n1052: \t\t\tb.Set(el.Name, el.Value)\n1053: \t\t}\n1054: \t}\n1055: }\n1056: \n1057: func (t *QueueManager) updateShardsLoop() {\n1058: \tdefer t.wg.Done()\n1059: \n1060: \tticker := time.NewTicker(shardUpdateDuration)\n1061: \tdefer ticker.Stop()\n1062: \tfor {\n1063: \t\tselect {\n1064: \t\tcase <-ticker.C:\n1065: \t\t\tdesiredShards := t.calculateDesiredShards()\n1066: \t\t\tif !t.shouldReshard(desiredShards) {\n1067: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1068: \t\t\t}\n1069: \t\t\t// Resharding can take some time, and we want this loop\n1070: \t\t\t// to stay close to shardUpdateDuration.\n1071: \t\t\tselect {\n1072: \t\t\tcase t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:\n1073: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n1074: \t\t\t\tt.numShards = desiredShards\n1075: \t\t\tdefault:\n1076: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Currently resharding, skipping.\")\n1077: \t\t\t}\n1078: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1079: \t\t\treturn\n1080: \t\t}\n1081: \t}\n1082: }\n1083: \n1084: // shouldReshard returns whether resharding should occur.\n1085: func (t *QueueManager) shouldReshard(desiredShards int) bool {\n1086: \tif desiredShards == t.numShards {\n1087: \t\treturn false\n1088: \t}\n1089: \t// We shouldn't reshard if Prometheus hasn't been able to send\n1090: \t// since the last time it checked if it should reshard.\n1091: \tminSendTimestamp := time.Now().Add(-1 * shardUpdateDuration).Unix()\n1092: \tlsts := t.lastSendTimestamp.Load()\n1093: \tif lsts < minSendTimestamp {\n1094: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, last successful send was beyond threshold\", \"lastSendTimestamp\", lsts, \"minSendTimestamp\", minSendTimestamp)\n1095: \t\treturn false\n1096: \t}\n1097: \tif disableTimestamp := t.reshardDisableEndTimestamp.Load(); time.Now().Unix() < disableTimestamp {\n1098: \t\tdisabledAt := time.Unix(t.reshardDisableStartTimestamp.Load(), 0)\n1099: \t\tdisabledFor := time.Until(time.Unix(disableTimestamp, 0))\n1100: \n1101: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, resharding is disabled while waiting for recoverable errors\", \"disabled_at\", disabledAt, \"disabled_for\", disabledFor)\n1102: \t\treturn false\n1103: \t}\n1104: \treturn true\n1105: }\n1106: \n1107: // calculateDesiredShards returns the number of desired shards, which will be\n1108: // the current QueueManager.numShards if resharding should not occur for reasons\n1109: // outlined in this functions implementation. It is up to the caller to reshard, or not,\n1110: // based on the return value.\n1111: func (t *QueueManager) calculateDesiredShards() int {\n1112: \tt.dataIn.tick()\n1113: \tt.dataOut.tick()\n1114: \tt.dataOutDuration.tick()\n1115: \n1116: \t// We use the number of incoming samples as a prediction of how much work we\n1117: \t// will need to do next iteration.  We add to this any pending samples\n1118: \t// (received - send) so we can catch up with any backlog. We use the average\n1119: \t// outgoing batch latency to work out how many shards we need.\n1120: \tvar (\n1121: \t\tdataInRate      = t.dataIn.rate()\n1122: \t\tdataOutRate     = t.dataOut.rate()\n1123: \t\tdataOutDuration = t.dataOutDuration.rate() / float64(time.Second)\n1124: \t\tdataPendingRate = dataInRate - dataOutRate\n1125: \t\thighestSent     = t.metrics.highestSentTimestamp.Get()\n1126: \t\thighestRecv     = t.metrics.highestTimestamp.Get()\n1127: \t\tdelay           = highestRecv - highestSent\n1128: \t\tdataPending     = delay * dataInRate\n1129: \t)\n1130: \n1131: \tif dataOutRate <= 0 {\n1132: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1133: \t}\n1134: \n1135: \tvar (\n1136: \t\t// When behind we will try to catch up on 5% of samples per second.\n1137: \t\tbacklogCatchup = 0.05 * dataPending\n1138: \t\t// Calculate Time to send one sample, averaged across all sends done this tick.\n1139: \t\ttimePerSample = dataOutDuration / dataOutRate\n1140: \t\tdesiredShards = timePerSample * (dataInRate + backlogCatchup)\n1141: \t)\n1142: \tt.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(desiredShards)\n1143: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards\",\n1144: \t\t\"dataInRate\", dataInRate,\n1145: \t\t\"dataOutRate\", dataOutRate,\n1146: \t\t\"dataPendingRate\", dataPendingRate,\n1147: \t\t\"dataPending\", dataPending,\n1148: \t\t\"dataOutDuration\", dataOutDuration,\n1149: \t\t\"timePerSample\", timePerSample,\n1150: \t\t\"desiredShards\", desiredShards,\n1151: \t\t\"highestSent\", highestSent,\n1152: \t\t\"highestRecv\", highestRecv,\n1153: \t)\n1154: \n1155: \t// Changes in the number of shards must be greater than shardToleranceFraction.\n1156: \tvar (\n1157: \t\tlowerBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. - shardToleranceFraction)\n1158: \t\tupperBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. + shardToleranceFraction)\n1159: \t)\n1160: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.updateShardsLoop\",\n1161: \t\t\"lowerBound\", lowerBound, \"desiredShards\", desiredShards, \"upperBound\", upperBound)\n1162: \n1163: \tdesiredShards = math.Ceil(desiredShards) // Round up to be on the safe side.\n1164: \tif lowerBound <= desiredShards && desiredShards <= upperBound {\n1165: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1166: \t}\n1167: \n1168: \tnumShards := int(desiredShards)\n1169: \t// Do not downshard if we are more than ten seconds back.\n1170: \tif numShards < t.numShards && delay > 10.0 {\n1171: \t\tt.logger.Debug(\"Not downsharding due to being too far behind\")\n1172: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1173: \t}\n1174: \n1175: \tswitch {\n1176: \tcase numShards > t.cfg.MaxShards:\n1177: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MaxShards\n1178: \tcase numShards < t.cfg.MinShards:\n1179: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MinShards\n1180: \t}\n1181: \treturn numShards\n1182: }\n1183: \n1184: func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n1185: \tdefer t.wg.Done()\n1186: \n1187: \tfor {\n1188: \t\tselect {\n1189: \t\tcase numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n1190: \t\t\t// We start the newShards after we have stopped (the therefore completely\n1191: \t\t\t// flushed) the oldShards, to guarantee we only every deliver samples in\n1192: \t\t\t// order.\n1193: \t\t\tt.shards.stop()\n1194: \t\t\tt.shards.start(numShards)\n1195: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1196: \t\t\treturn\n1197: \t\t}\n1198: \t}\n1199: }\n1200: \n1201: func (t *QueueManager) newShards() *shards {\n1202: \ts := &shards{\n1203: \t\tqm:   t,\n1204: \t\tdone: make(chan struct{}),\n1205: \t}\n1206: \treturn s\n1207: }\n1208: \n1209: type shards struct {\n1210: \tmtx sync.RWMutex // With the WAL, this is never actually contended.\n1211: \n1212: \tqm     *QueueManager\n1213: \tqueues []*queue\n1214: \t// So we can accurately track how many of each are lost during shard shutdowns.\n1215: \tenqueuedSamples    atomic.Int64\n1216: \tenqueuedExemplars  atomic.Int64\n1217: \tenqueuedHistograms atomic.Int64\n1218: \n1219: \t// Emulate a wait group with a channel and an atomic int, as you\n1220: \t// cannot select on a wait group.\n1221: \tdone    chan struct{}\n1222: \trunning atomic.Int32\n1223: \n1224: \t// Soft shutdown context will prevent new enqueues and deadlocks.\n1225: \tsoftShutdown chan struct{}\n1226: \n1227: \t// Hard shutdown context is used to terminate outgoing HTTP connections\n1228: \t// after giving them a chance to terminate.\n1229: \thardShutdown                    context.CancelFunc\n1230: \tsamplesDroppedOnHardShutdown \n1236: // start the shards; must be called before any call to enqueue.\n1237: func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n1238: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1239: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1240: \n1241: \ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)\n1242: \ts.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n1243: \n1244: \tnewQueues := make([]*queue, n)\n1245: \tfor i := range n {\n1246: \t\tnewQueues[i] = newQueue(s.qm.cfg.MaxSamplesPerSend, s.qm.cfg.Capacity)\n1247: \t}\n1248: \n1249: \ts.queues = newQueues\n1250: \n1251: \tvar hardShutdownCtx context.Context\n1252: \thardShutdownCtx, s.hardShutdown = context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n1253: \ts.softShutdown = make(chan struct{})\n1254: \ts.running.Store(int32(n))\n1255: \ts.done = make(chan struct{})\n1256: \ts.enqueuedSamples.Store(0)\n1257: \ts.enqueuedExemplars.Store(0)\n1258: \ts.enqueuedHistograms.Store(0)\n1259: \ts.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1260: \ts.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1261: \ts.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1262: \ts.metadataDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1263: \tfor i := range n {\n1264: \t\tgo s.runShard(hardShutdownCtx, i, newQueues[i])\n1265: \t}\n1266: }\n1267: \n1268: // stop the shards; subsequent call to enqueue will return false.\n1269: func (s *shards) stop() {\n1270: \t// Attempt a clean shutdown, but only wait flushDeadline for all the shards\n1271: \t// to cleanly exit. As we're doing RPCs, enqueue can block indefinitely.\n1272: \t// We must be able so call stop concurrently, hence we can only take the\n1273: \t// RLock here.\n1274: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1275: \tclose(s.softShutdown)\n1276: \ts.mtx.RUnlock()\n1277: \n1278: \t// Enqueue should now be unblocked, so we can take the write lock.  This\n1279: \t// also ensures we don't race with writes to the queues, and get a panic:\n1280: \t// send on closed channel.\n1281: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1282: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1283: \tfor _, queue := range s.queues {\n1284: \t\tgo queue.FlushAndShutdown(s.done)\n1285: \t}\n1286: \tselect {\n1287: \tcase <-s.done:\n1288: \t\treturn\n1289: \tcase <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):\n1290: \t}\n1291: \n1292: \t// Force an unclean shutdown.\n1293: \ts.hardShutdown()\n1294: \t<-s.done\n1295: \n1296: \t// Log error for any dropped samples, exemplars, or histograms.\n1297: \tlogDroppedError := func(t string, counter atomic.Uint32) {\n1298: \t\tif dropped := counter.Load(); dropped > 0 {\n1299: \t\t\ts.qm.logger.Error(fmt.Sprintf(\"Failed to flush all %s on shutdown\", t), \"count\", dropped)\n1300: \t\t}\n1301: \t}\n1302: \tlogDroppedError(\"samples\", s.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1303: \tlogDroppedError(\"exemplars\", s.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1304: \tlogDroppedError(\"histograms\", s.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1305: }\n1306: \n1307: // enqueue data (sample or exemplar). If the shard is full, shutting down, or\n1308: // resharding, it will return false; in this case, you should back off and\n1309: // retry. A shard is full when its configured capacity has been reached,\n1310: // specifically, when s.queues[shard] has filled its batchQueue channel and the\n1311: // partial batch has also been filled.\n1312: func (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n1313: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1314: \tdefer s.mtx.RUnlock()\n1315: \tshard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n1316: \tselect {\n1317: \tcase <-s.softShutdown:\n1318: \t\treturn false\n1319: \tdefault:\n1320: \t\tappended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)\n1321: \t\tif !appended {\n1322: \t\t\treturn false\n1323: \t\t}\n1324: \t\tswitch data.sType {\n1325: \t\tcase tSample:\n1326: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()\n1327: \t\t\ts.enqueuedSamples.Inc()\n1328: \t\tcase tExemplar:\n1329: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingExemplars.Inc()\n1330: \t\t\ts.enqueuedExemplars.Inc()\n1331: \t\tcase tHistogram, tFloatHistogram:\n1332: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingHistograms.Inc()\n1333: \t\t\ts.enqueuedHistograms.Inc()\n1334: \t\tdefault:\n1335: \t\t\treturn true\n1336: \t\t}\n1337: \t\ts.qm.metrics.highestTimestamp.Set(float64(data.timestamp / 1000))\n1338: \t\ts.qm.dataIn.incr(1)\n1339: \t\treturn true\n1340: \t}\n1341: }\n1342: \n1343: type queue struct {\n1344: \t// batchMtx covers operations appending to or publishing the partial batch.\n1345: \tbatchMtx   sync.Mutex\n1346: \tbatch      []timeSeries\n1347: \tbatchQueue chan []timeSeries\n1348: \n1349: \t// Since we know there are a limited number of batches out, using a stack\n1350: \t// is easy and safe so a sync.Pool is not necessary.\n1351: \t// poolMtx covers adding and removing batches from the batchPool.\n1352: \tpoolMtx   sync.Mutex\n1353: \tbatchPool [][]timeSeries\n1354: }\n1355: \n1356: type timeSeries struct {\n1357: \tseriesLabels   labels.Labels\n1358: \tvalue          float64\n1359: \thistogram      *histogram.Histogram\n1360: \tfloatHistogram *histogram.FloatHistogram\n1361: \tmetadata       *metadata.Metadata\n1362: \ttimestamp      int64\n1363: \texemplarLabels labels.Labels\n1364: \t// The type of series: sample, exemplar, or histogram.\n1365: \tsType seriesType\n1366: }\n1367: \n1368: type seriesType int\n1369: \n1370: const (\n1371: \ttSample seriesType = iota\n1372: \ttExemplar\n1373: \ttHistogram\n1374: \ttFloatHistogram\n1375: \ttMetadata\n1376: )\n1377: \n1378: func newQueue(batchSize, capacity int) *queue {\n1379: \tbatches := capacity / batchSize\n1380: \t// Always create an unbuffered channel even if capacity is configured to be\n1381: \t// less than max_samples_per_send.\n1382: \tif batches == 0 {\n1383: \t\tbatches = 1\n1384: \t}\n1385: \treturn &queue{\n1386: \t\tbatch:      make([]timeSeries, 0, batchSize),\n1387: \t\tbatchQueue: make(chan []timeSeries, batches),\n1388: \t\t// batchPool should have capacity for everything in the channel + 1 for\n1389: \t\t// the batch being processed.\n1390: \t\tbatchPool: make([][]timeSeries, 0, batches+1),\n1391: \t}\n1392: }\n1393: \n1394: // Append the timeSeries to the buffered batch. Returns false if it\n1395: // cannot be added and must be retried.\n1396: func (q *queue) Append(datum timeSeries) bool {\n1397: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1398: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1399: \t// TODO(cstyan): Check if metadata now means we've reduced the total # of samples\n1400: \t// we can batch together here, and if so find a way to not include metadata\n1401: \t// in the batch size calculation.\n1402: \t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n1403: \tq.batch = append(q.batch, datum)\n1404: \tif len(q.batch) == cap(q.batch) {\n1405: \t\tselect {\n1406: \t\tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1407: \t\t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(q.batch))\n1408: \t\t\treturn true\n1409: \t\tdefault:\n1410: \t\t\t// Remove the sample we just appended. It will get retried.\n1411: \t\t\tq.batch = q.batch[:len(q.batch)-1]\n1412: \t\t\treturn false\n1413: \t\t}\n1414: \t}\n1415: \treturn true\n1416: }\n1417: \n1418: func (q *queue) Chan() <-chan []timeSeries {\n1419: \treturn q.batchQueue\n1420: }\n1421: \n1422: // Batch returns the current batch and allocates a new batch.\n1423: func (q *queue) Batch() []timeSeries {\n1424: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1425: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1426: \tselect {\n1427: \tcase batch := <-q.batchQueue:\n1428: \t\treturn batch\n1429: \tdefault:\n1430: \t\tbatch := q.batch\n1431: \t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(batch))\n1432: \t\treturn batch\n1433: \t}\n1434: }\n1435: \n1436: // ReturnForReuse adds the batch buffer back to the internal pool.\n1437: func (q *queue) ReturnForReuse(batch []timeSeries) {\n1438: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1439: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1440: \tif len(q.batchPool) < cap(q.batchPool) {\n1441: \t\tq.batchPool = append(q.batchPool, batch[:0])\n1442: \t}\n1443: }\n1444: \n1445: // FlushAndShutdown stops the queue and flushes any samples. No appends can be\n1446: // made after this is called.\n1447: func (q *queue) FlushAndShutdown(done <-chan struct{}) {\n1448: \tfor q.tryEnqueueingBatch(done) {\n1449: \t\ttime.Sleep(time.Second)\n1450: \t}\n1451: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1452: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1453: \tq.batch = nil\n1454: \tclose(q.batchQueue)\n1455: }\n1456: \n1457: // tryEnqueueingBatch tries to send a batch if necessary. If sending needs to\n1458: // be retried it will return true.\n1459: func (q *queue) tryEnqueueingBatch(done <-chan struct{}) bool {\n1460: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1461: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1462: \tif len(q.batch) == 0 {\n1463: \t\treturn false\n1464: \t}\n1465: \n1466: \tselect {\n1467: \tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1468: \t\treturn false\n1469: \tcase <-done:\n1470: \t\t// The shard has been hard shut down, so no more samples can be sent.\n1471: \t\t// No need to try again as we will drop everything left in the queue.\n1472: \t\treturn false\n1473: \tdefault:\n1474: \t\t// The batchQueue is full, so we need to try again later.\n1475: \t\treturn true\n1476: \t}\n1477: }\n1478: \n1479: func (q *queue) newBatch(capacity int) []timeSeries {\n1480: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1481: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1482: \tbatches := len(q.batchPool)\n1483: \tif batches > 0 {\n1484: \t\tbatch := q.batchPool[batches-1]\n1485: \t\tq.batchPool = q.batchPool[:batches-1]\n1486: \t\treturn batch\n1487: \t}\n1488: \treturn make([]timeSeries, 0, capacity)\n1489: }\n1490: \n1491: func (s *shards) runShard(ctx context.Context, shardID int, queue *queue) {\n1492: \tdefer func() {\n1493: \t\tif s.running.Dec() == 0 {\n1494: \t\t\tclose(s.done)\n1495: \t\t}\n1496: \t}()\n1497: \n1498: \tshardNum := strconv.Itoa(shardID)\n1499: \tsymbolTable := writev2.NewSymbolTable()\n1500: \n1501: \t// Send batches of at most MaxSamplesPerSend samples to the remote storage.\n1502: \t// If we have fewer samples than that, flush them out after a deadline anyways.\n1503: \tvar (\n1504: \t\tmaxCount = s.qm.cfg.MaxSamplesPerSend\n1505: \n1506: \t\tpBuf    = proto.NewBuffer(nil)\n1507: \t\tpBufRaw []byte\n1508: \t\tencBuf  = compression.NewSyncEncodeBuffer()\n1509: \t)\n1510: \t// TODO(@tpaschalis) Should we also raise the max if we have WAL metadata?\n1511: \tif s.qm.sendExemplars {\n1512: \t\tmaxCount += := make([]prompb.TimeSeries, maxCount)\n1518: \tfor i := range pendingData {\n1519: \t\tpendingData[i].Samples = []prompb.Sample{{}}\n1520: \t\tif s.qm.sendExemplars {\n1521: {\n1532: \t\t\tselect {\n1533: \t\t\tcase <-timer.C:\n1534: \t\t\tdefault:\n1535: \t\t\t}\n1536: \t\t}\n1537: \t}\n1538: \tdefer stop()\n1539: \n1540: \tsendBatch := func(batch []timeSeries, protoMsg config.RemoteWriteProtoMsg, compr compression.Type, timer bool) {\n1541: \t\tswitch protoMsg {\n1542: \t\tcase config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1:\n1543: \t\t\tnPendingSamples, nPendingExemplars, {\n1562: \t\tselect {\n1563: \t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n1564: \t\t\t// In this case we drop all samples in the buffer and the queue.\n1565: \t\t\t// Remove them from pending and mark them as failed.\n1566: \t\t\tdroppedSamples := int(s.enqueuedSamples.Load())\n1567: \t\t\tdroppedExemplars := int(s.enqueuedExemplars.Load())\n1568: \t\t\tdroppedHistograms := int(s.enqueuedHistograms.Load())\n1569: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(droppedSamples))\n1570: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingExemplars.Sub(float64(droppedExemplars))\n1571: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingHistograms.Sub(float64(droppedHistograms))\n1572: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.failedSamplesTotal.Add(float64(droppedSamples))\n1573: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.failedExemplarsTotal.Add(float64(droppedExemplars))\n1574: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.failedHistogramsTotal.Add(float64(droppedHistograms))\n1575: \t\t\ts.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Add(uint32(droppedHistograms))\n1578: \t\t\treturn\n1579: \n1580: \t\tcase batch, ok := <-batchQueue:\n1581: \t\t\tif !ok {\n1582: \t\t\t\treturn\n1583: \t\t\t}\n1584: \n1585: \t\t\tsendBatch(batch, s.qm.protoMsg, s.qm.compr, false)\n1586: \t\t\t// TODO(bwplotka): Previously the return was between popular and send.\n1587: \t\t\t// Consider this when \t\t\ttimer.Reset(time.Duration(s.qm.cfg.BatchSendDeadline))\n1592: \n1593: \t\tcase <-timer.C:\n1594: \t\t\tbatch := queue.Batch()\n1595: \t\t\tif len(batch) > 0 {\n1596: \t\t\t\tsendBatch(batch, \n1604: func populateTimeSeries(batch []timeSeries, pendingData []prompb.TimeSeries, sendExemplars, sendNativeHistograms bool) (int, int, int) {\n1605: \tvar nPendingSamples, nPendingExemplars, nPendingHistograms int\n1606: \tfor nPending, d := range batch {\n1607: \t\tpendingData[nPending].Samples = pendingData[nPending].Samples[:0]\n1608: \t\tif sendExemplars {\n1609: pendingData[nPending].Histograms[:0]\n1613: \t\t}\n1614: \n1615: \t\t// Number of pending samples is limited by the fact that sendSamples (via sendSamplesWithBackoff)\n1616: \t\t// retries endlessly, so once we reach max samples, if we can never send to the endpoint we'll\n1617: \t\t// stop reading from the queue. \t\t\t\tLabels:    prompb.FromLabels(d.exemplarLabels, nil),\n1630: \t\t\t\tValue:     d.value,\n1631: \t\t\t\tTimestamp: d.timestamp,\n1632: \t\t\t})\n1633: \t\t\tnPendingExemplars++\n1634: \t\tcase \t\tcase tFloatHistogram:\n1638: \t\t\tpendingData[nPending].Histograms = append(pendingData[nPending].Histograms, prompb.FromFloatHistogram(d.timestamp, d.floatHistogram))\n1639: \t\t\tnPendingHistograms++\n1640: \t\t}\n1641: \t}\n1642: \treturn nPendingSamples, nPendingExemplars, nPendingHistograms\n1643: }\n1644: \n1645: func (s *shards) sendSamples(ctx context.Context, time.Since(begin))\n1649: \treturn err\n1650: }\n1651: \n1652: // TODO(bwplotka): DRY this (have one logic for both v1 and v2).\n1653: // See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14409\n1654: func (s *shards) sendV2Samples(ctx context.Context, samples []writev2.TimeSeries, labels []string, sampleCount, exemplarCount, time.Since(begin))\n1658: \treturn err\n1659: }\n1660: \n1661: func (s *shards) updateMetrics(_ context.Context, err error, sampleCount, exemplarCount, histogramCount, metadataCount int, rs WriteResponseStats, duration time.Duration) {\n1662: \t// Partial errors may happen -- account for that.\n1663: \tsampleDiff := sampleCount - rs.Samples\n1664: \tif sampleDiff > 0 {\n1665: \t\ts.qm.metrics.failedSamplesTotal.Add(float64(sampleDiff))\n1666: \t}\n1667: \thistogramDiff := histogramCount - rs.Histograms\n1668: \tif histogramDiff > 0 {\n1669: \t\ts.qm.metrics.failedHistogramsTotal.Add(float64(histogramDiff))\n1670: \t}\n1671: \texemplarDiff := exemplarCount - rs.Exemplars\n1672: \tif exemplarDiff > 0 {\n1673: \"failedExemplarCount\", exemplarDiff)\n1679: \t}\n1680: \n1681: \t// These counters are used to calculate the dynamic sharding, and as such\n1682: \t// should be maintained irrespective of success or failure.\n1683: \ts.qm.dataOut.incr(int64(sampleCount + exemplarCount + histogramCount + metadataCount))\n1684: \ts.qm.dataOutDuration.incr(int64(duration))\n1685: \ts.qm.lastSendTimestamp.Store(time.Now().Unix())\n1686: \n1687: \t// Pending samples/exemplars/histograms also should be subtracted, as an error means\n1688: \t// they will not be retried.\n1689: sendSamplesWithBackoff to the remote storage with backoff for recoverable errors.\n1698: func (s *shards) sendSamplesWithBackoff(ctx context.Context, samples []prompb.TimeSeries, sampleCount, func(int) error, onRetry func()) error {\n1982: \tbackoff := t.cfg.MinBackoff\n1983: \tsleepDuration := model.Duration(0)\n1984: \ttry := 0\n1985: \n1986: \tfor {\n1987: \t\tselect {\n1988: \t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n1989: \t\t\treturn ctx.Err()\n1990: \t\tdefault:\n1991: \t\t}\n1992: \n1993: \t\terr := attempt(try)\n1994: \n1995: \t\tif err == nil {\n1996: \t\t\treturn nil\n1997: \t\t}\n1998: \n1999: \t\t// If the error is unrecoverable, we should not retry.\n2000: \t\tvar backoffErr RecoverableError\n2001: \t\tif !errors.As(err, &backoffErr) {\n2002: \t\t\treturn err\n2003: \t\t}\n2004: \n2005: \t\tsleepDuration = backoff\n2006: \t\tswitch {\n2007: \t\tcase backoffErr.retryAfter > 0:\n2008: \t\t\tsleepDuration = backoffErr.retryAfter\n2009: \t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Retrying after duration specified by Retry-After header\", \"duration\", sleepDuration)\n2010: \t\tcase backoffErr.retryAfter < 0:\n2011: \t\t\tt.logger.Debug(\"retry-after cannot be in past, retrying using default backoff mechanism\")\n2012: \t\t}\n2013: \n2014: \t\t// We should never reshard for a recoverable error; increasing shards could\n2015: \t\t// make the problem worse, particularly if we're getting rate limited.\n2016: \t\t//\n2017: \t\t// reshardDisableTimestamp holds the unix timestamp until which resharding\n2018: \t\t// is disabled. We'll update that timestamp if the period we were just told\n2019: \t\t// to sleep for is newer than the existing disabled timestamp.\n2020: \t\treshardWaitPeriod := time.Now().Add(time.Duration(sleepDuration) * 2)\n2021: \t\tif oldTS, updated := setAtomicToNewer(&t.reshardDisableEndTimestamp, reshardWaitPeriod.Unix()); updated {\n2022: \t\t\t// If the old timestamp was in the past, then resharding was previously\n2023: \t\t\t// enabled. We want to track the time where it initially got disabled for\n2024: \t\t\t// logging purposes.\n2025: \t\t\tdisableTime := time.Now().Unix()\n2026: \t\t\tif oldTS < disableTime {\n2027: \t\t\t\tt.reshardDisableStartTimestamp.Store(disableTime)\n2028: \t\t\t}\n2029: \t\t}\n2030: \n2031: \t\tselect {\n2032: \t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n2033: \t\tcase <-time.After(time.Duration(sleepDuration)):\n2034: \t\t}\n2035: \n2036: \t\t// If we make it this far, we've encountered a recoverable error and will retry.\n2037: \t\tonRetry()\n2038: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Failed to send batch, retrying\", \"err\", err)\n2039: \n2040: \t\tbackoff = min(sleepDuration*2, t.cfg.MaxBackoff)\n2041: \n2042: \t\ttry++\n2043: \t}\n2044: }\n2045: \n2046: // setAtomicToNewer atomically sets a value to the newer int64 between itself\n2047: // and the provided newValue argument. setAtomicToNewer returns whether the\n2048: // atomic value was updated and what the previous value was.\n2049: func setAtomicToNewer(value *atomic.Int64, newValue int64) (previous int64, updated bool) {\n2050: \tfor {\n2051: \t\tcurrent := value.Load()\n2052: \t\tif current >= newValue {\n2053: \t\t\t// If the current stored value is newer than newValue; abort.\n2054: \t\t\treturn current, false\n2055: \t\t}\n2056: \n2057: \t\t// Try to swap the value. If the atomic value has changed, we loop back to\n2058: \t\t// the beginning until we've successfully swapped out the value or the\n2059: \t\t// value stored in it is newer than newValue.\n2060: \t\tif value.CompareAndSwap(current, newValue) {\n2061: \t\t\treturn current, true\n2062: \t\t}\n2063: \t}\n2064: }\n2065: \n2066: func buildTimeSeries(timeSeries []prompb.TimeSeries, filter func(prompb.TimeSeries) bool) (int64, int64, []prompb.TimeSeries, int, int, int) {\n2067: \tvar highest int64\n2068: \tvar lowest int64\n2069: \tvar droppedSamples, droppedExemplars, droppedHistograms int\n2070: \n2071: \tkeepIdx := 0\n2072: \tlowest = math.MaxInt64\n2073: \tfor i, ts := range timeSeries {\n2074: \t\tif filter != nil && filter(ts) {\n2075: \t\t\tif len(ts.Samples) > 0 {\n2076: \t\t\t\tdroppedHistograms++\n2083: \t\t\t}\n2084: \t\t\tcontinue\n2085: \t\t}\n2086: \n2087: \t\t// At the moment we only ever append a TimeSeries with a single sample or exemplar in it.\n2088: \t\tif {
  "content": "# Investigation Report: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure\n\n## Summary\nAfter Prometheus upgrades or target discovery changes, remote-write shards intermittently stall because samples enqueued during resharding are permanently dropped during hard shutdown when the flush deadline expires, violating the delivery guarantee and causing metrics to show stuck pending samples.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Location**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go` - Resharding logic (lines 1184-1199, 1269-1305, 1491-1602)\n\n**Mechanism**:\nWhen resharding occurs (e.g., target discovery adds/removes targets), the `reshardLoop()` function:\n\n1. Calls `t.shards.stop()` to shutdown old shards\n2. Calls `t.shards.start(numShards)` to create new shards with different queue counts\n\nDuring `stop()` (lines 1269-1305):\n- Line 1275: Closes `softShutdown` channel (prevents new enqueues)\n- Line 1281-1284: Takes write lock and initiates `FlushAndShutdown()` on all queues\n- Line 1289: Waits up to `flushDeadline` (default 1 minute) for graceful flush\n- Line 1293: If timeout exceeded, calls `hardShutdown()` unconditionally\n\nWhen `hardShutdown()` is called (cancels `hardShutdownCtx`):\n- All `runShard()` goroutines receive `ctx.Done()` signal (line 1563)\n- Lines 1566-1577: **All pending samples are dropped without being sent**\n- No re-attempt or recovery mechanism exists\n\n**The Critical Bug**:\nSamples in flight when the flush deadline expires are permanently lost because:\n1. They're dropped during hard shutdown (line 1575-1577)\n2. They're never re-enqueued to new shards\n3. The metrics counters are decremented (lines 1569-1571) but the samples are gone\n4. New shards start with a different hash distribution, so old shard data cannot be recovered\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References\n\n**Resharding Trigger** (lines 1057-1082):\n```\nstorage/remote/queue_manager.go:1072-1074\n  case t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:\n      t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n      t.numShards = desiredShards\n```\n\n**Resharding Loop** (lines 1184-1199):\n```\nstorage/remote/queue_manager.go:1189-1194\n  case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n      t.shards.stop()           // Initiates flush\n      t.shards.start(numShards) // Creates new shards (NEW HASH DISTRIBUTION)\n```\n\n**Hard Shutdown Path** (lines 1286-1294):\n```\nstorage/remote/queue_manager.go:1286-1294\n  select {\n  case <-s.done:\n      return                    // Graceful flush succeeded\n  case <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):\n      // Timeout - force shutdown\n  }\n  s.hardShutdown()             // Cancel context\n  <-s.done\n```\n\n**Sample Drop on Hard Shutdown** (lines 1563-1578):\n```\nstorage/remote/queue_manager.go:1563-1578\n  case <-ctx.Done():\n      // In this case we drop all samples in the buffer and the queue.\n      // Remove them from pending and mark them as failed.\n      droppedSamples := int(s.enqueuedSamples.Load())\n      s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(droppedSamples))\n      s.qm.metrics.failedSamplesTotal.Add(float64(droppedSamples))\n      s.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown.Add(uint32(droppedSamples))\n      return\n```\n\n**Queue Flushing with Timeout** (lines 1447-1455):\n```\nstorage/remote/queue_manager.go:1447-1455\n  func (q *queue) FlushAndShutdown(done <-chan struct{}) {\n      for q.tryEnqueueingBatch(done) {\n          time.Sleep(time.Second)\n      }\n      q.batchMtx.Lock()\n      q.batch = nil\n      close(q.batchQueue)\n  }\n```\n\nWhen `done` is closed (hard shutdown triggered), `tryEnqueueingBatch()` (lines 1469-1472) abandons the batch:\n```\nstorage/remote/queue_manager.go:1469-1472\n  case <-done:\n      // The shard has been hard shut down, so no more samples can be sent.\n      // No need to try again as we will drop everything left in the queue.\n      return false\n```\n\n### CHANGELOG Evidence\nLine 451 of CHANGELOG.md notes a related fix:\n```\n* [ENHANCEMENT] Remote Write: Disable resharding during active retry backoffs #13562\n```\nThis indicates the Prometheus maintainers recognized resharding causes issues and added logic to disable it during recoverable errors (see `shouldReshard()` lines 1085-1105).\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **Primary**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`\n   - `reshardLoop()` - orchestrates shard replacement\n   - `shards.stop()` - initiates graceful flush with timeout\n   - `shards.start()` - creates new shards with new queue distribution\n   - `runShard()` - executes hard shutdown and drops samples\n\n2. **Secondary**: Metrics system\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - shows stuck pending samples\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_failed_samples_total` - incremented but samples are gone\n   - Related: `shards_desired`, `numShards`, `highestTimestamp` metrics\n\n3. **Timing Dependencies**:\n   - Default `flushDeadline`: typically 1 minute (user configurable)\n   - `shardUpdateDuration`: 30 seconds (checks if resharding needed)\n   - `BatchSendDeadline`: typically 5-10 seconds per batch\n\n## Why the Issue is Intermittent\n\n1. **Load-Dependent**: High sample ingestion rates cause batches to accumulate in queues, requiring more time to flush all pending work\n2. **Network-Dependent**: Slow remote-write endpoint responses delay flush completion\n3. **Target Discovery Timing**: Resharding happens at fixed 30-second intervals; coinciding with high load or network issues increases failure probability\n4. **Flush Deadline**: Default 1 minute is often insufficient when:\n   - Many shards (each with separate flush operations)\n   - Large batches (more time to serialize/send)\n   - Slow remote endpoint (network latency)\n\n**Example Failure Scenario**:\n- T=0s: Target discovery changes, 100 targets added \u2192 need resharding from 4\u21928 shards\n- T=30s: reshardLoop detects change, initiates stop()\n- T=31s: 8 old shards each have 1000 pending samples in flight to slow endpoint\n- T=85s: Only 6 of 8 shards have flushed (2 still waiting for sends to complete)\n- T=90s: flushDeadline (60s) expires \u2192 hardShutdown() triggered\n- T=91s: 2000+ samples dropped, never reach remote storage\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n1. **Option A (Preferred)**: Extend or make flush deadline dynamic based on shard count and queue depth\n2. **Option B**: Implement graceful queue draining into new shards instead of dropping samples\n3. **Option C**: Temporarily disable resharding (via `shouldReshard()` logic) when queues have high pending samples\n4. **Option D**: Store dropped samples back into WAL for retry instead of discarding\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\nTo confirm root cause in a failing deployment:\n\n1. # Investigation Report: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure

## Summary
After Prometheus upgrades or target discovery changes, remote-write shards intermittently stall because samples enqueued during resharding are permanently dropped during hard shutdown when the flush deadline expires, violating the delivery guarantee and causing metrics to show stuck pending samples.

## Root Cause

**Location**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go` - Resharding logic (lines 1184-1199, 1269-1305, 1491-1602)

**Mechanism**:
When resharding occurs (e.g., target discovery adds/removes targets), the `reshardLoop()` function:

1. Calls `t.shards.stop()` to shutdown old shards
2. Calls `t.shards.start(numShards)` to create new shards with different queue counts

During `stop()` (lines 1269-1305):
- Line 1275: Closes `softShutdown` channel (prevents new enqueues)
- Line 1281-1284: Takes write lock and initiates `FlushAndShutdown()` on all queues
- Line 1289: Waits up to `flushDeadline` (default 1 minute) for graceful flush
- Line 1293: If timeout exceeded, calls `hardShutdown()` unconditionally

When `hardShutdown()` is called (cancels `hardShutdownCtx`):
- All `runShard()` goroutines receive `ctx.Done()` signal (line 1563)
- Lines 1566-1577: **All pending samples are dropped without being sent**
- No re-attempt or recovery mechanism exists

**The Critical Bug**:
Samples in flight when the flush deadline expires are permanently lost because:
1. They're dropped during hard shutdown (line 1575-1577)
2. They're never re-enqueued to new shards
3. The metrics counters are decremented (lines 1569-1571) but the samples are gone
4. New shards start with a different hash distribution, so old shard data cannot be recovered

## Evidence

### Code References

**Resharding Trigger** (lines 1057-1082):
``
... (truncated)
